          </b>

           palaugov.pw

      <p>
       <b>
        Palau
       </b>
       (
       <span class="nowrap">
        <span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt">
         <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">
          /
          <span style="border-bottom:1px dotted">
           <span title="'p' in 'pie'">
            p
           </span>
           <span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">
            ə
           </span>
           <span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">
            ˈ
           </span>
           <span title="'l' in 'lie'">
            l
           </span>
           <span title="/aʊ/: 'ou' in 'mouth'">
            aʊ
           </span>
          </span>
          /
         </a>
        </span>
        <small class="nowrap">
         (
         <span class="unicode haudio">
          <span class="fn">
           <span style="white-space:nowrap">
            <a href="/wiki/File:En-us-Palau.ogg" title="About this sound">
             <img alt="About this sound" data-file-height="20" data-file-width="20" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" width="11"/>
            </a>
           </span>
           <a class="internal" href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/e/ea/En-us-Palau.ogg" title="En-us-Palau.ogg">
            listen
           </a>
          </span>
         </span>
         )
        </small>
       </span>
       , historically
       <b>
        Belau
       </b>
       or
       <b>
        Pelew
       </b>
       ), officially the
       <b>
        Republic of Palau
       </b>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/Palauan_language" title="Palauan language">
        Palauan
       </a>
       :
       <i>
        <span lang="pau">
         Beluu er a Belau
        </span>
       </i>
       ),
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5">
        <a href="#cite_note-5">
         [5]
        </a>
       </sup>
       is an
       <a href="/wiki/Island_country" title="Island country">
        island country
       </a>
       located in the western
       <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Ocean" title="Pacific Ocean">
        Pacific Ocean
       </a>
       . The country contains approximately 340 islands, forming the western chain of the
       <a href="/wiki/Caroline_Islands" title="Caroline Islands">
        Caroline Islands
       </a>
       in
       <a href="/wiki/Micronesia" title="Micronesia">
        Micronesia
       </a>
       , and has an area of 466 square kilometers (180 sq mi).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6">
        <a href="#cite_note-6">
         [6]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The most populous island is
       <a href="/wiki/Koror" title="Koror">
        Koror
       </a>
       . The capital
       <a href="/wiki/Ngerulmud" title="Ngerulmud">
        Ngerulmud
       </a>
       is located on the nearby island of
       <a href="/wiki/Babeldaob" title="Babeldaob">
        Babeldaob
       </a>
       , in
       <a href="/wiki/Melekeok" title="Melekeok">
        Melekeok State
       </a>
       . Palau shares
       <a href="/wiki/Maritime_boundary" title="Maritime boundary">
        maritime boundaries
       </a>
       with
       <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">
        Indonesia
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">
        Philippines
       </a>
       , and the
       <a href="/wiki/Federated_States_of_Micronesia" title="Federated States of Micronesia">
        Federated States of Micronesia
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       The country was originally settled approximately 3,000 years ago by migrants from the
       <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">
        Philippines
       </a>
       and sustained a
       <a href="/wiki/Negrito" title="Negrito">
        Negrito
       </a>
       population until around 900 years ago. The islands were first explored by Europeans in the 16th century, and were made part of the
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_East_Indies" title="Spanish East Indies">
        Spanish East Indies
       </a>
       in 1574. Following Spain's defeat in the
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish%E2%80%93American_War" title="Spanish–American War">
        Spanish–American War
       </a>
       in 1898, the islands were sold to
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Imperial_Germany" title="Imperial Germany">
        Imperial Germany
       </a>
       in 1899 under the terms of the
       <a href="/wiki/German%E2%80%93Spanish_Treaty_(1899)" title="German–Spanish Treaty (1899)">
        German–Spanish Treaty
       </a>
       , where they were administered as part of
       <a href="/wiki/German_New_Guinea" title="German New Guinea">
        German New Guinea
       </a>
       . The
       <a href="/wiki/Imperial_Japanese_Navy" title="Imperial Japanese Navy">
        Imperial Japanese Navy
       </a>
       conquered Palau during
       <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">
        World War I
       </a>
       , and the islands were later made a part of the Japanese-ruled
       <a href="/wiki/South_Pacific_Mandate" title="South Pacific Mandate">
        South Pacific Mandate
       </a>
       by the
       <a href="/wiki/League_of_Nations" title="League of Nations">
        League of Nations
       </a>
       . During
       <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">
        World War II
       </a>
       , skirmishes, including the major
       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Peleliu" title="Battle of Peleliu">
        Battle of Peleliu
       </a>
       , were fought between American and Japanese troops as part of the
       <a href="/wiki/Mariana_and_Palau_Islands_campaign" title="Mariana and Palau Islands campaign">
        Mariana and Palau Islands campaign
       </a>
       . Along with other
       <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Islands" title="Pacific Islands">
        Pacific Islands
       </a>
       , Palau was made a part of the
       <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">
        United States
       </a>
       -governed
       <a href="/wiki/Trust_Territory_of_the_Pacific_Islands" title="Trust Territory of the Pacific Islands">
        Trust Territory of the Pacific Islands
       </a>
       in 1947. Having voted against joining the Federated States of Micronesia in 1979, the islands gained full sovereignty in 1994 under a
       <a href="/wiki/Compact_of_Free_Association" title="Compact of Free Association">
        Compact of Free Association
       </a>
       with the United States.
      </p>
      <p>
       Politically, Palau is a
       <a href="/wiki/Presidential_system" title="Presidential system">
        presidential
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Republic" title="Republic">
        republic
       </a>
       in
       <a href="/wiki/Associated_state" title="Associated state">
        free association
       </a>
       with the United States, which provides defense, funding, and access to social services. Legislative power is concentrated in the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bicameral" title="Bicameral">
        bicameral
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Palau_National_Congress" title="Palau National Congress">
        Palau National Congress
       </a>
       .
       <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Palau" title="Economy of Palau">
        Palau's economy
       </a>
       is based mainly on
       <a href="/wiki/Tourism" title="Tourism">
        tourism
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Subsistence_agriculture" title="Subsistence agriculture">
        subsistence agriculture
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Fishing" title="Fishing">
        fishing
       </a>
       , with a significant portion of
       <a href="/wiki/Gross_national_product" title="Gross national product">
        gross national product
       </a>
       (GNP) derived from foreign aid. The country uses the
       <a href="/wiki/United_States_dollar" title="United States dollar">
        United States dollar
       </a>
       as its currency. The islands' culture mixes Micronesian,
       <a href="/wiki/Melanesia" title="Melanesia">
        Melanesian
       </a>
       , Asian, and Western elements. Ethnic Palauans, the majority of the population, are of mixed Micronesian, Melanesian, and
       <a href="/wiki/Austronesia" title="Austronesia">
        Austronesian
       </a>
       descent. A smaller proportion of the population is descended from
       <a href="/wiki/Japanese_people" title="Japanese people">
        Japanese
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Filipino_people" title="Filipino people">
        Filipino
       </a>
       settlers. The country's two
       <a href="/wiki/Official_language" title="Official language">
        official languages
       </a>
       are
       <a href="/wiki/Palauan_language" title="Palauan language">
        Palauan
       </a>
       (a member of the wider
       <a href="/wiki/Sunda%E2%80%93Sulawesi_languages" title="Sunda–Sulawesi languages">
        Sunda–Sulawesi language group
       </a>
       ) and
       <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">
        English
       </a>
       , with
       <a href="/wiki/Japanese_language" title="Japanese language">
        Japanese
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Sonsorolese_language" title="Sonsorolese language">
        Sonsorolese
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Tobian_language" title="Tobian language">
        Tobian
       </a>
       recognized as
       <a href="/wiki/Regional_language" title="Regional language">
        regional languages
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
      </p>

      <p>

      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">
        Etymology
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Palau&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       The name for the islands in the
       <a href="/wiki/Palauan_language" title="Palauan language">
        Palauan language
       </a>
       ,
       <i>
        Belau
       </i>
       , likely derives from either the Palauan word for "village",
       <i>
        beluu
       </i>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7">
        <a href="#cite_note-7">
         [7]
        </a>
       </sup>
       or from
       <i>
        aibebelau
       </i>
       ("indirect replies"), relating to a creation myth.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8">
        <a href="#cite_note-8">
         [8]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The name "Palau" entered the
       <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">
        English language
       </a>
       from the
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">
        Spanish
       </a>
       <i>
        Los Palaos
       </i>
       , via the
       <a href="/wiki/German_language" title="German language">
        German
       </a>
       <i>
        Palau
       </i>
       . An archaic name for the islands in English was the "Pelew Islands".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9">
        <a href="#cite_note-9">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <i>
        Palau
       </i>
       is unrelated to
       <i>
        Pulau
       </i>
       , which is a
       <a href="/wiki/Malay_language" title="Malay language">
        Malay
       </a>
       word meaning "island" found in a number of place names in the region.
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="History">
        History
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Palau&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation">
       <tr>
        <td class="mbox-image">
         <div style="width:52px">

          </a>
         </div>
        </td>
        <td class="mbox-text">
         <div class="mbox-text-span">

          <b>
           needs additional citations for
           <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">

           </a>
          </b>

          <span class="hide-when-compact">

      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/History_of_Palau" title="History of Palau">
        History of Palau
       </a>
      </div>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Early_history">
        Early history
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Palau&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Early history">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Palau was originally settled between the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/3rd_millennium_BCE" title="3rd millennium BCE">
        3rd
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2nd_millennium_BCE" title="2nd millennium BCE">
        2nd millennia BCE
       </a>
       , most likely from
       <a href="/wiki/Austronesia" title="Austronesia">
        Austronesia
       </a>
       or
       <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">
        Indonesia
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10">
        <a href="#cite_note-10">
         [10]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The islands sustained a population of short-statured
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Melanesian" title="Melanesian">
        Melanesian
       </a>
       or
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pygmy_people" title="Pygmy people">
        Pygmy people
       </a>
       until the 12th century, when they were replaced.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2013)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       The modern
       <a href="/wiki/Micronesia" title="Micronesia">
        Micronesian
       </a>
       population, judging by its language, may have come from the
       <a href="/wiki/Sunda_Islands" title="Sunda Islands">
        Sunda Islands
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Sonsorol" title="Sonsorol">
        Sonsorol
       </a>
       , part of the
       <a href="/wiki/Southwest_Islands_(Palau)" title="Southwest Islands (Palau)">
        Southwest Islands
       </a>
       , an island chain approximately 600 kilometers (370 mi) from the main island chain of Palau, was sighted by Europeans as early as 1522, when the Spanish mission of the
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Trinidad_(ship)" title="Trinidad (ship)">
         Trinidad
        </a>
       </i>
       , the flagship of
       <a href="/wiki/Ferdinand_Magellan" title="Ferdinand Magellan">
        Ferdinand Magellan
       </a>
       's voyage of circumnavigation, sighted two small islands around the
       <a href="/wiki/5th_parallel_north" title="5th parallel north">
        5th parallel north
       </a>
       , naming them "San Juan".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11">
        <a href="#cite_note-11">
         [11]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Islas_Marianas_Palaos_y_Carolinas.JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="489" data-file-width="902" height="119" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Islas_Marianas_Palaos_y_Carolinas.JPG/220px-Islas_Marianas_Palaos_y_Carolinas.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Islas_Marianas_Palaos_y_Carolinas.JPG/330px-Islas_Marianas_Palaos_y_Carolinas.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Islas_Marianas_Palaos_y_Carolinas.JPG/440px-Islas_Marianas_Palaos_y_Carolinas.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Islas_Marianas_Palaos_y_Carolinas.JPG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Map of 1888 showing the Spanish East Indies, being part of it Palau Islands (map without Philippines)
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       After the conquest of the Philippines in 1565 by the
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Empire" title="Spanish Empire">
        Spanish Empire
       </a>
       , the archipelago of Palau became part of the territory of the
       <a href="/wiki/Captaincy_General_of_the_Philippines" title="Captaincy General of the Philippines">
        Captaincy General of the Philippines
       </a>
       , established in 1574 as part of the
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_East_Indies" title="Spanish East Indies">
        Spanish East Indies
       </a>
       with the capital based in the colonial centre in
       <a href="/wiki/Manila" title="Manila">
        Manila
       </a>
       . However, the Spanish presence only began to express with
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Evangelization" title="Evangelization">
        evangelization
       </a>
       , began at the end of the 17th century, and its dominance began to take shape in the 18th century.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="After_16th_century">
        After 16th century
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Palau&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: After 16th century">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       The conscious discovery of Palau came a century later in 1697, when a group of Palauans were shipwrecked on the Philippine island of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Samar_Island" title="Samar Island">
        Samar
       </a>
       to the northwest. They were interviewed by the
       <a href="/wiki/Czechs" title="Czechs">
        Czech
       </a>
       missionary
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Paul_Klein_(missionary)" title="Paul Klein (missionary)">
        Paul Klein
       </a>
       on 28 December 1696. Klein was able to draw the first map of Palau based on the Palauans' representation of their home islands that they made with an arrangement of 87 pebbles on the beach. Klein reported his findings to the
       <a href="/wiki/Society_of_Jesus" title="Society of Jesus">
        Jesuit
       </a>
       Superior General in a letter sent in June 1697,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12">
        <a href="#cite_note-12">
         [12]
        </a>
       </sup>
       equaling to the discovery of Palau.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Spanish_era">
        Spanish era
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Palau&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Spanish era">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       This map and the letter caused a vast interest in the new islands. Another letter written by Fr. Andrés Serrano was sent to Europe in 1705, essentially copying the information given by Klein. The letters resulted in three unsuccessful Jesuit attempts to travel to Palau from
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spanish_Philippines" title="Spanish Philippines">
        Spanish Philippines
       </a>
       in 1700, 1708 and 1709. The islands were first visited by the Jesuit expedition led by Francisco Padilla on 30 November 1710. The expedition ended with the stranding of the two priests, Jacques Du Beron and Joseph Cortyl, on the coast of Sonsorol, because the mother ship
       <i>
        Santísima Trinidad
       </i>
       was driven to
       <a href="/wiki/Mindanao" title="Mindanao">
        Mindanao
       </a>
       by a storm. Another ship was sent from
       <a href="/wiki/Guam" title="Guam">
        Guam
       </a>
       in 1711 to save them only to capsize, causing the death of three more Jesuit priests. The failure of these missions gave Palau the original Spanish name
       <i>
        Islas Encantadas
       </i>
       (Enchanted Islands).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13">
        <a href="#cite_note-13">
         [13]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Despite these early misfortunes, the
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Empire" title="Spanish Empire">
        Spanish Empire
       </a>
       later came to dominate the islands.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2015)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Colonial_era">
        Colonial era
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Palau&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Colonial era">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Koror_chiefs_in_1915.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="352" data-file-width="472" height="164" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Koror_chiefs_in_1915.jpg/220px-Koror_chiefs_in_1915.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Koror_chiefs_in_1915.jpg/330px-Koror_chiefs_in_1915.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Koror_chiefs_in_1915.jpg/440px-Koror_chiefs_in_1915.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Koror_chiefs_in_1915.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Koror chiefs in 1915
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       British traders became prominent visitors to Palau in the 18th century, followed by expanding Spanish influence in the 19th century. Following its defeat in the
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish%E2%80%93American_War" title="Spanish–American War">
        Spanish–American War
       </a>
       , Spain sold Palau and most of the rest of the Caroline Islands to the
       <a href="/wiki/German_Empire" title="German Empire">
        German Empire
       </a>
       in 1899 pursuant to the
       <a href="/wiki/German%E2%80%93Spanish_Treaty_(1899)" title="German–Spanish Treaty (1899)">
        German–Spanish Treaty (1899)
       </a>
       . During
       <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">
        World War I
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Empire_of_Japan" title="Empire of Japan">
        Japanese Empire
       </a>
       annexed the islands after seizing them from Germany in 1914. Following World War I, the
       <a href="/wiki/League_of_Nations" title="League of Nations">
        League of Nations
       </a>
       formally placed the islands under Japanese administration as part of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nanyo_(Japanese_mandated_territory)" title="Nanyo (Japanese mandated territory)">
        South Pacific Mandate
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="United_States_era">
        United States era
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Palau&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: United States era">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       During
       <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">
        World War II
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">
        United States
       </a>
       captured Palau from Japan in 1944 after the costly
       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Peleliu" title="Battle of Peleliu">
        Battle of Peleliu
       </a>
       , when more than 2,000 Americans and 10,000 Japanese were killed. The islands passed formally to the United States under
       <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">
        United Nations
       </a>
       auspices in 1947 as part of the
       <a href="/wiki/Trust_Territory_of_the_Pacific_Islands" title="Trust Territory of the Pacific Islands">
        Trust Territory of the Pacific Islands
       </a>
       established pursuant to
       <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council_Resolution_21" title="United Nations Security Council Resolution 21">
        Security Council Resolution 21
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Independence">
        Independence
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Palau&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Independence">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:TTPI_High_Commissioner_and_staff.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="449" data-file-width="640" height="154" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/TTPI_High_Commissioner_and_staff.jpg/220px-TTPI_High_Commissioner_and_staff.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/TTPI_High_Commissioner_and_staff.jpg/330px-TTPI_High_Commissioner_and_staff.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/TTPI_High_Commissioner_and_staff.jpg/440px-TTPI_High_Commissioner_and_staff.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:TTPI_High_Commissioner_and_staff.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         TTPI High Commissioner and staff, 1960s
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Four of the Trust Territory districts joined together and formed the
       <a href="/wiki/Federated_States_of_Micronesia" title="Federated States of Micronesia">
        Federated States of Micronesia
       </a>
       in 1979, but the districts of Palau and the
       <a href="/wiki/Marshall_Islands" title="Marshall Islands">
        Marshall Islands
       </a>
       declined to participate. Palau, the westernmost cluster of the
       <a href="/wiki/Caroline_Islands" title="Caroline Islands">
        Carolines
       </a>
       , instead opted for independent status in 1978. It approved a new constitution and became the Republic of Palau in 1981.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14">
        <a href="#cite_note-14">
         [14]
        </a>
       </sup>
       It signed a
       <a href="/wiki/Compact_of_Free_Association" title="Compact of Free Association">
        Compact of Free Association
       </a>
       with the
       <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">
        United States
       </a>
       in 1982. After eight referenda and an amendment to the Palauan constitution, the Compact was ratified in 1993. The Compact went into effect on 1 October 1994,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15">
        <a href="#cite_note-15">
         [15]
        </a>
       </sup>
       marking Palau
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/De_jure" title="De jure">
         de jure
        </a>
       </i>
       independent, although it had been
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/De_facto" title="De facto">
         de facto
        </a>
       </i>
       independent since 25 May 1994, when the trusteeship ended.
      </p>
      <p>
       Legislation making Palau an "offshore" financial center was passed by the Senate in 1998. In 2001, Palau passed its first
       <a href="/wiki/Bank_regulation" title="Bank regulation">
        bank regulation
       </a>
       and anti-
       <a href="/wiki/Money_laundering" title="Money laundering">
        money laundering
       </a>
       laws.
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Politics_and_government">
        Politics and government
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Palau&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Politics and government">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Palau" title="Politics of Palau">
        Politics of Palau
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Capitol,_Melekeok,_Palau.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2314" data-file-width="3474" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Capitol%2C_Melekeok%2C_Palau.jpg/220px-Capitol%2C_Melekeok%2C_Palau.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Capitol%2C_Melekeok%2C_Palau.jpg/330px-Capitol%2C_Melekeok%2C_Palau.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Capitol%2C_Melekeok%2C_Palau.jpg/440px-Capitol%2C_Melekeok%2C_Palau.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Capitol,_Melekeok,_Palau.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Capitol of Palau, the seat of government.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Palau is a
       <a href="/wiki/Multi-party_system" title="Multi-party system">
        multi-party
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Representative_democracy" title="Representative democracy">
        democratic
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Republic" title="Republic">
        republic
       </a>
       . The
       <a href="/wiki/President_of_Palau" title="President of Palau">
        President of Palau
       </a>
       is both
       <a href="/wiki/Head_of_state" title="Head of state">
        head of state
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Head_of_government" title="Head of government">
        head of government
       </a>
       .
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Executive_power" title="Executive power">
        Executive power
       </a>
       is exercised by the government, while
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Legislative_power" title="Legislative power">
        legislative power
       </a>
       is vested in both the government and the
       <a href="/wiki/Palau_National_Congress" title="Palau National Congress">
        Palau National Congress
       </a>
       . The
       <a href="/wiki/Judiciary_of_Palau" title="Judiciary of Palau">
        judiciary
       </a>
       is independent of the executive and the legislature. Palau adopted a constitution in 1981.
      </p>
      <p>
       The governments of the United States and Palau concluded a
       <a href="/wiki/Compact_of_Free_Association" title="Compact of Free Association">
        Compact of Free Association
       </a>
       in 1986, similar to compacts that the United States had entered into with the
       <a href="/wiki/Federated_States_of_Micronesia" title="Federated States of Micronesia">
        Federated States of Micronesia
       </a>
       and the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Republic_of_the_Marshall_Islands" title="Republic of the Marshall Islands">
        Republic of the Marshall Islands
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gao-08-732_p7_16-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-gao-08-732_p7-16">
         [16]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The compact entered into force on 1 October 1994, concluding Palau's transition from trusteeship to independence
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gao-08-732_p7_16-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-gao-08-732_p7-16">
         [16]
        </a>
       </sup>
       as the last portion of the
       <a href="/wiki/Trust_Territory_of_the_Pacific_Islands" title="Trust Territory of the Pacific Islands">
        Trust Territory of the Pacific Islands
       </a>
       to secure its independence pursuant to
       <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council_Resolution_956" title="United Nations Security Council Resolution 956">
        Security Council Resolution 956
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Compact_of_Free_Association" title="Compact of Free Association">
        Compact of Free Association
       </a>
       between the United States and Palau
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17">
        <a href="#cite_note-17">
         [17]
        </a>
       </sup>
       sets forth the free and voluntary association of their governments. It primarily focuses on the issues of government, economic, security and defense relations.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18">
        <a href="#cite_note-18">
         [18]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Palau has no independent military, relying on the United States for its defense. Under the compact, the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/American_military" title="American military">
        American military
       </a>
       was granted access to the islands for 50 years. The
       <a href="/wiki/United_States_Navy" title="United States Navy">
        U.S. Navy
       </a>
       role is minimal, limited to a handful of Navy
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Seabee_(US_Navy)" title="Seabee (US Navy)">
        Seabees
       </a>
       (construction engineers). The
       <a href="/wiki/United_States_Coast_Guard" title="United States Coast Guard">
        U.S. Coast Guard
       </a>
       patrols in national waters.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations">
        Foreign relations
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Palau&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Foreign relations">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Palau" title="Foreign relations of Palau">
        Foreign relations of Palau
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       As a sovereign nation, Palau conducts its own foreign relations.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gao-08-732_p7_16-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-gao-08-732_p7-16">
         [16]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Since independence, Palau has established diplomatic relations with a number of nations, including many of its Pacific neighbors, like
       <a href="/wiki/Micronesia" title="Micronesia">
        Micronesia
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">
        Philippines
       </a>
       . On 29 November 1994, the
       <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council" title="United Nations Security Council">
        United Nations Security Council
       </a>
       passed
       <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council_Resolution_963" title="United Nations Security Council Resolution 963">
        Resolution 963
       </a>
       recommending Palau's admission to the
       <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">
        United Nations
       </a>
       . The
       <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly" title="United Nations General Assembly">
        United Nations General Assembly
       </a>
       approved admission for Palau pursuant to Resolution 49/63 on 15 December 1994.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19">
        <a href="#cite_note-19">
         [19]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Palau has since joined several other international organizations. In September 2006, Palau hosted the first Taiwan-Pacific Allies Summit. Its President has made official visits to other Pacific countries, including Japan.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20">
        <a href="#cite_note-20">
         [20]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The United States maintains a diplomatic delegation and an embassy in Palau, but most aspects of the countries' relationship have to do with Compact-funded projects, which are the responsibility of the U.S.
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Department_of_the_Interior" title="Department of the Interior">
        Department of the Interior
       </a>
       's
       <a href="/wiki/Office_of_Insular_Affairs" title="Office of Insular Affairs">
        Office of Insular Affairs
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21">
        <a href="#cite_note-21">
         [21]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In international politics, Palau often votes with the United States with respect to
       <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly" title="United Nations General Assembly">
        United Nations General Assembly
       </a>
       resolutions.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22">
        <a href="#cite_note-22">
         [22]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Palau is a member of the
       <a href="/wiki/Nauru_Agreement" title="Nauru Agreement">
        Nauru Agreement
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-radioaustralia_23-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-radioaustralia-23">
         [23]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In 1981, Palau voted for the world's first nuclear-free constitution. This constitution banned the use, storage and disposal of
       <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_weapon" title="Nuclear weapon">
        nuclear
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Chemical_weapon" title="Chemical weapon">
        toxic chemical
       </a>
       , gas and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Biological_weapon" title="Biological weapon">
        biological weapons
       </a>
       without first being approved by a ¾ majority in a referendum.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24">
        <a href="#cite_note-24">
         [24]
        </a>
       </sup>
       This ban delayed Palau's transition to independence, because while negotiating the Compact, the U.S. insisted on the option to operate
       <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_marine_propulsion" title="Nuclear marine propulsion">
        nuclear propelled vessels
       </a>
       and store nuclear weapons within the territory,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25">
        <a href="#cite_note-25">
         [25]
        </a>
       </sup>
       prompting campaigns for independence and denuclearisation.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26">
        <a href="#cite_note-26">
         [26]
        </a>
       </sup>
       After several referendums that failed to achieve a ¾ majority, the people of Palau finally approved the Compact in 1994.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27">
        <a href="#cite_note-27">
         [27]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28">
        <a href="#cite_note-28">
         [28]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">
        Philippines
       </a>
       , a neighboring ally of Palau to the west, has expressed its intent to back Palau if ever it wishes to join
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ASEAN" title="ASEAN">
        ASEAN
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2017)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In June 2009, Palau announced that it would
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Uyghur_captives_in_Guantanamo" title="Uyghur captives in Guantanamo">
        accept up to seventeen
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Uyghurs" title="Uyghurs">
        Uyghurs
       </a>
       that had previously been detained by the American military at
       <a href="/wiki/Guantanamo_Bay_detention_camp" title="Guantanamo Bay detention camp">
        Guantanamo Bay
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ctv2009-06-10_29-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Ctv2009-06-10-29">
         [29]
        </a>
       </sup>
       with some American compensation for the cost of their upkeep.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Abc2009-06-10_30-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Abc2009-06-10-30">
         [30]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Only one of the Uyghurs initially agreed to resettlement,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rnzi2009-06-30_31-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Rnzi2009-06-30-31">
         [31]
        </a>
       </sup>
       but by the end of October, six of the seventeen had been transferred to Palau.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Afp2009-10-31_32-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Afp2009-10-31-32">
         [32]
        </a>
       </sup>
       An aid agreement with the United States, finalized in January 2010, was reported to be unrelated to the Uyghur agreement.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33">
        <a href="#cite_note-33">
         [33]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">
        Administrative divisions
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Palau&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Administrative divisions">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:377px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:States_of_Palau.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1518" data-file-width="1154" height="493" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/States_of_Palau.jpg/375px-States_of_Palau.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/States_of_Palau.jpg/563px-States_of_Palau.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/States_of_Palau.jpg/750px-States_of_Palau.jpg 2x" width="375"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:States_of_Palau.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The sixteen states of Palau.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/States_of_Palau" title="States of Palau">
        States of Palau
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       Palau is divided into sixteen
       <a href="/wiki/Constituent_state" title="Constituent state">
        states
       </a>
       (until 1984 called municipalities). These are listed below with their areas (in square kilometers) and 2012 Census populations:
      </p>

      <p>
       Historically, Palau's
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rock_Islands_(Palau)" title="Rock Islands (Palau)">
        Rock Islands
       </a>
       have been part of the State of Koror.
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Palau-CIA_WFB_Map.png">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="350" data-file-width="326" height="236" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Palau-CIA_WFB_Map.png/220px-Palau-CIA_WFB_Map.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/7/74/Palau-CIA_WFB_Map.png 1.5x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Palau-CIA_WFB_Map.png" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Republic of Palau.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Maritime_law_enforcement">
        Maritime law enforcement
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Palau&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Maritime law enforcement">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Palau employs 18 marine police officers to patrol the nation's 230,000 square mile
       <a href="/wiki/Exclusive_economic_zone" title="Exclusive economic zone">
        exclusive economic zone
       </a>
       . They employ a donated Australian patrol boat, the
       <i>
        Remeliik
       </i>
       , to hunt for poachers and unlicensed fishermen. Two small fiberglass boats are used for littoral operations. They are based on
       <a href="/wiki/Koror" title="Koror">
        Koror
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34">
        <a href="#cite_note-34">
         [34]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">
        Geography
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Palau&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Geography">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Palau" title="Geography of Palau">
        Geography of Palau
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       Palau's territory consists of an
       <a href="/wiki/Archipelago" title="Archipelago">
        archipelago
       </a>
       located in the
       <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Ocean" title="Pacific Ocean">
        Pacific Ocean
       </a>
       . Its most populous
       <a href="/wiki/Island" title="Island">
        islands
       </a>
       are
       <a href="/wiki/Angaur" title="Angaur">
        Angaur
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Babeldaob" title="Babeldaob">
        Babeldaob
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Koror" title="Koror">
        Koror
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Peleliu" title="Peleliu">
        Peleliu
       </a>
       . The latter three lie together within the same
       <a href="/wiki/Coral_reef" title="Coral reef">
        barrier reef
       </a>
       , while Angaur is an oceanic island several miles to the south. About two-thirds of the
       <a href="/wiki/Population" title="Population">
        population
       </a>
       live on Koror.
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Coral" title="Coral">
        coral
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Atoll" title="Atoll">
        atoll
       </a>
       of
       <a href="/wiki/Kayangel" title="Kayangel">
        Kayangel
       </a>
       is north of these islands, while the uninhabited
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rock_Islands_(Palau)" title="Rock Islands (Palau)">
        Rock Islands
       </a>
       (about 200) are west of the main island group. A remote group of six islands, known as the
       <a href="/wiki/Southwest_Islands_(Palau)" title="Southwest Islands (Palau)">
        Southwest Islands
       </a>
       , some 375 miles (604 km) from the main islands, make up the states of Hatohobei and Sonsorol.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">
        Climate
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Palau&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Climate">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Palau has a
       <a href="/wiki/Tropical_rainforest_climate" title="Tropical rainforest climate">
        tropical rainforest climate
       </a>
       with an annual
       <a href="/wiki/Arithmetic_mean" title="Arithmetic mean">
        mean
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Temperature" title="Temperature">
        temperature
       </a>
       of 28 °C (82 °F).
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rainfall" title="Rainfall">
        Rainfall
       </a>
       is heavy throughout the
       <a href="/wiki/Year" title="Year">
        year
       </a>
       , averaging 3,800 mm (150 in). The average
       <a href="/wiki/Humidity" title="Humidity">
        humidity
       </a>
       is 82% and, although rain falls more frequently between July and October, there is still much
       <a href="/wiki/Sunlight" title="Sunlight">
        sunshine
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclone" title="Tropical cyclone">
        Typhoons
       </a>
       are rare, as Palau lies outside the main typhoon zone. The strongest typhoon that struck Palau since reliable records was
       <a href="/wiki/Typhoon_Haiyan" title="Typhoon Haiyan">
        Typhoon Haiyan
       </a>
       in
       <a href="/wiki/2013_Pacific_typhoon_season" title="2013 Pacific typhoon season">
        2013
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35">
        <a href="#cite_note-35">
         [35]
        </a>
       </sup>
       A mandatory
       <a href="/wiki/Emergency_evacuation" title="Emergency evacuation">
        emergency evacuation
       </a>
       was issued for
       <a href="/wiki/Kayangel" title="Kayangel">
        Kayangel
       </a>
       . A
       <a href="/wiki/Storm_surge" title="Storm surge">
        storm surge
       </a>
       damaged several houses. Despite residents' refusal to evacuate safely, no fatalities or major injuries were reported.
      </p>
      <div style="clear:both;">
      </div>

          </a>
