      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Environment">
        Environment
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Palau&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Environment">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Palau-rock-islands20071222.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="915" data-file-width="1680" height="120" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Palau-rock-islands20071222.jpg/220px-Palau-rock-islands20071222.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Palau-rock-islands20071222.jpg/330px-Palau-rock-islands20071222.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Palau-rock-islands20071222.jpg/440px-Palau-rock-islands20071222.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Palau-rock-islands20071222.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rock_Islands_(Palau)" title="Rock Islands (Palau)">
          Rock Islands
         </a>
         in Palau.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Palau_2008030818_4709_(2347767520).jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2314" data-file-width="3474" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Palau_2008030818_4709_%282347767520%29.jpg/220px-Palau_2008030818_4709_%282347767520%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Palau_2008030818_4709_%282347767520%29.jpg/330px-Palau_2008030818_4709_%282347767520%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Palau_2008030818_4709_%282347767520%29.jpg/440px-Palau_2008030818_4709_%282347767520%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Palau_2008030818_4709_(2347767520).jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         An aerial view of limestone islands.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       While much of Palau remains free of environmental degradation, areas of concern include illegal
       <a href="/wiki/Blast_fishing" title="Blast fishing">
        dynamite fishing
       </a>
       , inadequate
       <a href="/wiki/Waste_management" title="Waste management">
        solid waste disposal
       </a>
       facilities in
       <a href="/wiki/Koror" title="Koror">
        Koror
       </a>
       and extensive
       <a href="/wiki/Sand" title="Sand">
        sand
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Coral" title="Coral">
        coral
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Dredging" title="Dredging">
        dredging
       </a>
       in the Palau
       <a href="/wiki/Lagoon" title="Lagoon">
        lagoon
       </a>
       . As with other Pacific island nations,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sea-level_rise" title="Sea-level rise">
        rising sea level
       </a>
       presents a major environmental threat. Inundation of low-lying areas threatens coastal
       <a href="/wiki/Vegetation" title="Vegetation">
        vegetation
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Agriculture" title="Agriculture">
        agriculture
       </a>
       , and an already insufficient
       <a href="/wiki/Water_supply" title="Water supply">
        water supply
       </a>
       .
       <a href="/wiki/Wastewater_treatment" title="Wastewater treatment">
        Wastewater treatment
       </a>
       is a problem, along with the handling of
       <a href="/wiki/Toxic_waste" title="Toxic waste">
        toxic waste
       </a>
       from
       <a href="/wiki/Fertilizer" title="Fertilizer">
        fertilizers
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Biocide" title="Biocide">
        biocides
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Saltwater_crocodile" title="Saltwater crocodile">
        Saltwater crocodiles
       </a>
       are also indigenous to Palau and occur in varying numbers throughout the various
       <a href="/wiki/Mangrove" title="Mangrove">
        mangroves
       </a>
       and in parts of the rock islands. Although this
       <a href="/wiki/Species" title="Species">
        species
       </a>
       is generally considered extremely dangerous, there has only been one fatal human attack in Palau within modern history, and that was in the 1960s. In Palau, the largest crocodile measured in at 4.5 meters (15 ft).
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2011)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The nation is also vulnerable to
       <a href="/wiki/Earthquake" title="Earthquake">
        earthquakes
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Volcano" title="Volcano">
        volcanic activity
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclone" title="Tropical cyclone">
        tropical storms
       </a>
       . Palau already has a problem with inadequate
       <a href="/wiki/Water_supply" title="Water supply">
        water supply
       </a>
       and limited
       <a href="/wiki/Agricultural_land" title="Agricultural land">
        agricultural areas
       </a>
       to support its
       <a href="/wiki/Population" title="Population">
        population
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       On 5 November 2005, President Tommy E. Remengesau, Jr. took the lead on a regional environmental initiative called the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Micronesia_challenge" title="Micronesia challenge">
        Micronesia challenge
       </a>
       , which would conserve 30% of near-shore coastal waters and 20% of
       <a href="/wiki/Forest" title="Forest">
        forest land
       </a>
       by 2020. Following Palau, the initiative was joined by the
       <a href="/wiki/Federated_States_of_Micronesia" title="Federated States of Micronesia">
        Federated States of Micronesia
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Marshall_Islands" title="Marshall Islands">
        Marshall Islands
       </a>
       , and the
       <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">
        U.S.
       </a>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Territory_(geographic_region)" title="Territory (geographic region)">
        territories
       </a>
       of
       <a href="/wiki/Guam" title="Guam">
        Guam
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Northern_Mariana_Islands" title="Northern Mariana Islands">
        Northern Mariana Islands
       </a>
       . Together, this combined region represents nearly 5% of the marine area of the
       <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Ocean" title="Pacific Ocean">
        Pacific Ocean
       </a>
       and 7% of its
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Coastline" title="Coastline">
        coastline
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Sanctuary">
        Sanctuary
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Palau&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Sanctuary">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       On 25 September 2009, Palau announced that it would create the world's first
       <a href="/wiki/Shark_sanctuary" title="Shark sanctuary">
        shark sanctuary
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Palau_creates_world's_first_shark_haven_37-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Palau_creates_world's_first_shark_haven-37">
         [37]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Palau banned all commercial
       <a href="/wiki/Shark" title="Shark">
        shark
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Fishing" title="Fishing">
        fishing
       </a>
       within the waters of its
       <a href="/wiki/Exclusive_economic_zone" title="Exclusive economic zone">
        exclusive economic zone (EEZ)
       </a>
       . The sanctuary protects about 600,000 square kilometers (230,000 sq mi) of
       <a href="/wiki/World_Ocean" title="World Ocean">
        ocean
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38">
        <a href="#cite_note-38">
         [38]
        </a>
       </sup>
       a similar size to
       <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">
        France
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Palau's_EEZ_becomes_shark_sanctuary_39-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Palau's_EEZ_becomes_shark_sanctuary-39">
         [39]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-World's_first_shark_sanctuary_created_by_Pacific_island_of_Palau_40-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-World's_first_shark_sanctuary_created_by_Pacific_island_of_Palau-40">
         [40]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-France-Size_Shark_Sanctuary_Created_--_A_First_41-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-France-Size_Shark_Sanctuary_Created_--_A_First-41">
         [41]
        </a>
       </sup>
       President
       <a href="/wiki/Johnson_Toribiong" title="Johnson Toribiong">
        Johnson Toribiong
       </a>
       announced the sanctuary at a meeting of the
       <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">
        United Nations
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Palau's_EEZ_becomes_shark_sanctuary_39-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Palau's_EEZ_becomes_shark_sanctuary-39">
         [39]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Palau_creates_shark_sanctuary_to_protect_tourism_and_prevent_overfishing_42-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Palau_creates_shark_sanctuary_to_protect_tourism_and_prevent_overfishing-42">
         [42]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Palau_to_Ban_Shark_Fishing_43-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Palau_to_Ban_Shark_Fishing-43">
         [43]
        </a>
       </sup>
       President Toribiong proposed a worldwide ban on fishing for sharks.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Palau's_EEZ_becomes_shark_sanctuary_39-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-Palau's_EEZ_becomes_shark_sanctuary-39">
         [39]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In 2012, Palau received the Future Policy Award from
       <a href="/wiki/World_Future_Council" title="World Future Council">
        World Future Council
       </a>
       , because "Palau is a global leader in protecting marine ecosystems".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44">
        <a href="#cite_note-44">
         [44]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">
        Economy
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Palau&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Economy">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Palau" title="Economy of Palau">
        Economy of Palau
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       Palau's
       <a href="/wiki/Economy" title="Economy">
        economy
       </a>
       consists primarily of
       <a href="/wiki/Tourism" title="Tourism">
        tourism
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Subsistence_agriculture" title="Subsistence agriculture">
        subsistence agriculture
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Fishing" title="Fishing">
        fishing
       </a>
       . Tourist activity focuses on
       <a href="/wiki/Scuba_diving" title="Scuba diving">
        scuba diving
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Snorkeling" title="Snorkeling">
        snorkeling
       </a>
       in the islands' rich marine environment, including its
       <a href="/wiki/Coral_reef" title="Coral reef">
        barrier reefs
       </a>
       ' walls and
       <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">
        World War II
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Shipwreck" title="Shipwreck">
        wrecks
       </a>
       . The government is the largest
       <a href="/wiki/Employment" title="Employment">
        employer
       </a>
       , relying heavily on
       <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">
        U.S.
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Aid" title="Aid">
        financial assistance
       </a>
       . Business and tourist arrivals numbered some 50,000 in
       <a href="/wiki/Fiscal_year" title="Fiscal year">
        fiscal year
       </a>
       2000–2001.
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Japan_Palau_Friendship_Bridge.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="575" data-file-width="800" height="158" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Japan_Palau_Friendship_Bridge.jpg/220px-Japan_Palau_Friendship_Bridge.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Japan_Palau_Friendship_Bridge.jpg/330px-Japan_Palau_Friendship_Bridge.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Japan_Palau_Friendship_Bridge.jpg/440px-Japan_Palau_Friendship_Bridge.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Japan_Palau_Friendship_Bridge.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Koror%E2%80%93Babeldaob_Bridge" title="Koror–Babeldaob Bridge">
          Koror–Babeldaob Bridge
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Population" title="Population">
        population
       </a>
       enjoys a
       <a href="/wiki/Per_capita_income" title="Per capita income">
        per capita income
       </a>
       twice that of
       <a href="/wiki/Micronesia" title="Micronesia">
        Micronesia
       </a>
       as a whole. Long-term prospects for the key tourist sector have been greatly bolstered by the expansion of
       <a href="/wiki/Air_travel" title="Air travel">
        air travel
       </a>
       in the
       <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Rim" title="Pacific Rim">
        Pacific
       </a>
       , the rising prosperity of leading
       <a href="/wiki/East_Asia" title="East Asia">
        East Asian
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Country" title="Country">
        countries
       </a>
       and the willingness of
       <a href="/wiki/Alien_(law)" title="Alien (law)">
        foreigners
       </a>
       to
       <a href="/wiki/Investment" title="Investment">
        finance
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Infrastructure" title="Infrastructure">
        infrastructure
       </a>
       development.
      </p>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Airline" title="Airline">
        Air service
       </a>
       has at times been spotty.
       <a href="/wiki/Palau_Micronesia_Air" title="Palau Micronesia Air">
        Palau Micronesia Air
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Asian_Spirit" title="Asian Spirit">
        Asian Spirit
       </a>
       and
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Pacific_Flier&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Pacific Flier (page does not exist)">
        Pacific Flier
       </a>
       provided service to the
       <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">
        Philippines
       </a>
       and other destinations at various times during the 2000s, but all suspended service.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45">
        <a href="#cite_note-45">
         [45]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a href="/wiki/United_Airlines" title="United Airlines">
        United Airlines
       </a>
       now provides near-daily service to and from
       <a href="/wiki/Guam" title="Guam">
        Guam
       </a>
       , and once-weekly service to
       <a href="/wiki/Yap" title="Yap">
        Yap
       </a>
       . Also,
       <a href="/wiki/Delta_Air_Lines" title="Delta Air Lines">
        Delta Air Lines
       </a>
       provides service three times per week to
       <a href="/wiki/Tokyo" title="Tokyo">
        Tokyo
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       In November 2006,
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Palau_Saving_Bank&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Palau Saving Bank (page does not exist)">
        Palau Saving Bank
       </a>
       officially announced
       <a href="/wiki/Bankruptcy" title="Bankruptcy">
        bankruptcy
       </a>
       . On 13 December 2006, the
       <a href="/wiki/Palau_Horizon" title="Palau Horizon">
        Palau Horizon
       </a>
       reported that 641
       <a href="/wiki/Deposit_account" title="Deposit account">
        depositors
       </a>
       had been affected. Among them, 398 held less than US$5,000, with the remainder ranging from US$5,000 to US$2 million. On 12 December 79 affected people received compensation. Mr. Toribiong said, "The fund for the payout came from the balance of Palau government's loan from
       <a href="/wiki/Taiwan" title="Taiwan">
        Taiwan
       </a>
       ." From a total of US$1 million, which originally was for assisting Palau's development, US$955,000 was left at the time of bankruptcy. Toribiong requested the Taiwanese government use the balance to repay its loans. Taiwan agreed to the request. The compensation would include those who held less than US$4,000 in an account.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46">
        <a href="#cite_note-46">
         [46]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Income_tax" title="Income tax">
        income tax
       </a>
       has three
       <a href="/wiki/Tax_bracket" title="Tax bracket">
        brackets
       </a>
       with
       <a href="/wiki/Progressive_tax" title="Progressive tax">
        progressive
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Tax_rate" title="Tax rate">
        rates
       </a>
       of 9.3 percent, 15 percent, and 19.6 percent respectively.
       <a href="/wiki/Corporate_tax" title="Corporate tax">
        Corporate tax
       </a>
       is four percent, and the
       <a href="/wiki/Sales_tax" title="Sales tax">
        sales tax
       </a>
       is zero. There are no
       <a href="/wiki/Property_tax" title="Property tax">
        property taxes
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       <br/>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Transportation">
        Transportation
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Palau&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Transportation">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Palau_International_Airport_1.JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1536" data-file-width="2048" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Palau_International_Airport_1.JPG/220px-Palau_International_Airport_1.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Palau_International_Airport_1.JPG/330px-Palau_International_Airport_1.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Palau_International_Airport_1.JPG/440px-Palau_International_Airport_1.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Palau_International_Airport_1.JPG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Palau_International_Airport" title="Palau International Airport">
          Palau International Airport
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Palau_International_Airport" title="Palau International Airport">
        Palau International Airport
       </a>
       provides scheduled
       <a href="/wiki/Direct_flight" title="Direct flight">
        direct flights
       </a>
       with
       <a href="/wiki/Antonio_B._Won_Pat_International_Airport" title="Antonio B. Won Pat International Airport">
        Guam
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Ninoy_Aquino_International_Airport" title="Ninoy Aquino International Airport">
        Manila
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Incheon_International_Airport" title="Incheon International Airport">
        Seoul
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Taoyuan_International_Airport" title="Taoyuan International Airport">
        Taipei
       </a>
       and since December 2010,
       <a href="/wiki/Narita_International_Airport" title="Narita International Airport">
        Tokyo-Narita
       </a>
       .
       <a href="/wiki/Palau_Pacific_Airways" title="Palau Pacific Airways">
        Palau Pacific Airways
       </a>
       also has charter flights to and from
       <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong_International_Airport" title="Hong Kong International Airport">
        Hong Kong
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Macau_International_Airport" title="Macau International Airport">
        Macau
       </a>
       . In addition, the states of
       <a href="/wiki/Angaur" title="Angaur">
        Angaur
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Peleliu" title="Peleliu">
        Peleliu
       </a>
       have regular service to
       <a href="/wiki/International_flight" title="International flight">
        international destinations
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Freight, military and cruise ships often call at Malakal Harbor, on
       <a href="/wiki/Malakal_Island" title="Malakal Island">
        Malakal Island
       </a>
       outside Koror. The country has no
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Railway" title="Railway">
        railways
       </a>
       , and of the 61 km or 38 mi of
       <a href="/wiki/Highway" title="Highway">
        highways
       </a>
       , only 36 km or 22 mi are
       <a href="/wiki/Road_surface" title="Road surface">
        paved
       </a>
       .
       <a href="/wiki/Driving" title="Driving">
        Driving
       </a>
       is on the right and the
       <a href="/wiki/Speed_limit" title="Speed limit">
        speed limit
       </a>
       is 40 km/h (25 mph).
       <a href="/wiki/Taxicab" title="Taxicab">
        Taxis
       </a>
       are available in Koror. They are not metered and
       <a href="/wiki/Fare" title="Fare">
        fares
       </a>
       are negotiable. Only Koror offers
       <a href="/wiki/Transit_bus" title="Transit bus">
        bus service
       </a>
       . Transportation between islands mostly relies on private
       <a href="/wiki/Boat" title="Boat">
        boats
       </a>
       and domestic
       <a href="/wiki/Airline" title="Airline">
        air services
       </a>
       . However, there are some
       <a class="external text" href="http://outofyourcomfortzone.net/all-the-schedules-and-prices-for-palaus-state-boat-between-koror-peleliu-and-angaur/" rel="nofollow">
        state run boats
       </a>
       between islands as a cheaper alternative.
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">
        Demographics
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Palau&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Demographics">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Palau" title="Demographics of Palau">
        Demographics of Palau
       </a>
      </div>
      <table class="toccolours" style="width:15em;border-spacing: 0;float:right;clear:right;margin:0 0 1em 1em;">
       <tr>
        <th class="navbox-title" colspan="2" style="padding:0.25em;font-size:110%">
         Historical population
        </th>
       </tr>
       <tr style="font-size:95%">
        <th style="border-bottom:1px solid black;padding:1px;width:auto">
         Year
        </th>
        <th style="border-bottom:1px solid black;padding:1px 2px;text-align:right">
         <abbr title="Population">
          Pop.
         </abbr>
        </th>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <th style="text-align:center;padding:1px">
         <a href="/wiki/1970_United_States_Census" title="1970 United States Census">
          1970
         </a>
        </th>
        <td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">
         11,210
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <th style="text-align:center;padding:1px">
         <a href="/wiki/1980_United_States_Census" title="1980 United States Census">
          1980
         </a>
        </th>
        <td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">
         12,116
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <th style="text-align:center;padding:1px">
         <a href="/wiki/1990_United_States_Census" title="1990 United States Census">
          1990
         </a>
        </th>
        <td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">
         15,122
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <th style="text-align:center;padding:1px">
         <a href="/wiki/2000_United_States_Census" title="2000 United States Census">
          2000
         </a>
        </th>
        <td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">
         21,000
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <p>
       The population of Palau is approximately 21,503, of whom 73% are native Palauans of mixed
       <a href="/wiki/Melanesia" title="Melanesia">
        Melanesian
       </a>
       , and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Austronesian" title="Austronesian">
        Austronesian
       </a>
       descent. There are many Asian communities within Palau.
       <a href="/wiki/Filipinos_in_Palau" title="Filipinos in Palau">
        Filipinos
       </a>
       form the largest Asian group and second largest ethnic group in the country. There are significant numbers of
       <a href="/wiki/Chinese_in_Palau" title="Chinese in Palau">
        Chinese
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Koreans_in_Micronesia" title="Koreans in Micronesia">
        Koreans
       </a>
       . There are also smaller numbers of Palauans of mixed or full
       <a href="/wiki/Japanese_settlement_in_Palau" title="Japanese settlement in Palau">
        Japanese ancestry
       </a>
       . Smaller numbers of
       <a href="/wiki/Bangladeshi_diaspora" title="Bangladeshi diaspora">
        Bangladeshi
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Non_Resident_Nepali" title="Non Resident Nepali">
        Nepalese
       </a>
       migrant workers and their descendants who came to the islands during the late 1900s can also be found. Most Palauans of Asian origin came during the late 1900s with many Filipinos, Chinese, Bangladeshis and Nepalese coming to Palau as unskilled workers and professionals.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47">
        <a href="#cite_note-47">
         [47]
        </a>
       </sup>
       There are also small numbers of
       <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">
        Europeans
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">
        Americans
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tobi_AKK_Villagers.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="500" data-file-width="340" height="324" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Tobi_AKK_Villagers.jpg/220px-Tobi_AKK_Villagers.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Tobi_AKK_Villagers.jpg/330px-Tobi_AKK_Villagers.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/3/39/Tobi_AKK_Villagers.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Tobi_AKK_Villagers.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Tobi villagers.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">
        Languages
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Palau&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Languages">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       The official languages of Palau are
       <a href="/wiki/Palauan_language" title="Palauan language">
        Palauan
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">
        English
       </a>
       , except for two states (
       <a href="/wiki/Sonsorol" title="Sonsorol">
        Sonsorol
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Hatohobei" title="Hatohobei">
        Hatohobei
       </a>
       ) where the local language,
       <a href="/wiki/Sonsorolese_language" title="Sonsorolese language">
        Sonsorolese
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Tobian_language" title="Tobian language">
        Tobian
       </a>
       , respectively, along with Palauan, is official.
       <a href="/wiki/Japanese_language" title="Japanese language">
        Japanese
       </a>
       is spoken by some older Palauans and is an official language in the State of
       <a href="/wiki/Angaur" title="Angaur">
        Angaur
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cia-factbook_48-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-cia-factbook-48">
         [48]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ethnologue_49-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-ethnologue-49">
         [49]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Including second-language speakers, more people speak English than Palauan in Palau
       <a class="external autonumber" href="http://www.ethnologue.com/country/pw/languages/" rel="nofollow">
        [1]
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">
        Religion
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Palau&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Religion">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Palau" title="Religion in Palau">
        Religion in Palau
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       According to 2015 estimates 45.3% of the population is
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Church" title="Roman Catholic Church">
        Roman Catholic
       </a>
       , 34.9%
       <a href="/wiki/Protestantism" title="Protestantism">
        Protestant
       </a>
       , 6.9%
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Seventh-day_Adventism" title="Seventh-day Adventism">
        Seventh-day Adventist
       </a>
       , 5.7%
       <a href="/wiki/Modekngei" title="Modekngei">
        Modekngei
       </a>
       and 3.0% Muslim.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cia_1-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-cia-1">
         [1]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In 2009, the small
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jewish" title="Jewish">
        Jewish
       </a>
       community sent two cyclists to the 18th
       <a href="/wiki/Maccabiah_Games" title="Maccabiah Games">
        Maccabiah Games
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50">
        <a href="#cite_note-50">
         [50]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The German and Japanese occupations of Palau both subsidized missionaries to follow the Spanish. Germans sent Roman Catholic and Protestant, Japanese sent Shinto and Buddhist, and Spaniards sent Roman Catholic missionaries as they controlled Palau. Three quarters of the population are
       <a href="/wiki/Christian" title="Christian">
        Christians
       </a>
       (mainly
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Church" title="Roman Catholic Church">
        Roman Catholics
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Protestants" title="Protestants">
        Protestants
       </a>
       ), while
       <a href="/wiki/Modekngei" title="Modekngei">
        Modekngei
       </a>
       (a combination of Christianity, traditional Palauan religion and fortune telling) and the ancient Palauan religion are commonly observed. Japanese rule brought
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mahayana_Buddhism" title="Mahayana Buddhism">
        Mahayana Buddhism
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Shinto" title="Shinto">
        Shinto
       </a>
       to Palau, which were the majority religions among Japanese settlers. However, following Japan's World War II defeat, the remaining Japanese largely converted to Christianity, while the remainder continued to observe Buddhism, but stopped practicing Shinto rites.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51">
        <a href="#cite_note-51">
         [51]
        </a>
       </sup>
       There are also approximately 400 Bengali Muslims in Palau, and recently a few
       <a href="/wiki/Uyghurs" title="Uyghurs">
        Uyghurs
       </a>
       detained in
       <a href="/wiki/Guantanamo_Bay_detention_camp" title="Guantanamo Bay detention camp">
        Guantanamo Bay
       </a>
       were allowed to settle in the island nation.
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">
        Culture
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Palau&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Culture">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Palau" title="Music of Palau">
        Music of Palau
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Palauan_language" title="Palauan language">
        Palauan language
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:A_traditional_Palauan_hut,_2012.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2543" data-file-width="3814" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/A_traditional_Palauan_hut%2C_2012.jpg/220px-A_traditional_Palauan_hut%2C_2012.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/A_traditional_Palauan_hut%2C_2012.jpg/330px-A_traditional_Palauan_hut%2C_2012.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/A_traditional_Palauan_hut%2C_2012.jpg/440px-A_traditional_Palauan_hut%2C_2012.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:A_traditional_Palauan_hut,_2012.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         A traditional Palauan hut (2012)
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Palauan society follows a very strict
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Matrilineal" title="Matrilineal">
        matrilineal
       </a>
       system. Matrilineal practices are seen in nearly every aspect of Palauan traditions, especially in funeral, marriage, inheritance and the passing of traditional titles.
      </p>
      <p>
       The cuisine includes local foods such as
       <a href="/wiki/Cassava" title="Cassava">
        cassava
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Taro" title="Taro">
        taro
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Yam_(vegetable)" title="Yam (vegetable)">
        yam
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Potato" title="Potato">
        potato
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Fish" title="Fish">
        fish
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Pork" title="Pork">
        pork
       </a>
       .
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Western_cuisine" title="Western cuisine">
        Western cuisine
       </a>
       is favored among young Palauans and the locals are joined by foreign tourists. The rest of Micronesia is similar with much less tourism, leading to fewer restaurants.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2017)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       Tourists eat mainly at their hotels on such islands. Some local foods include an alcoholic drink made from coconut on the tree; the drink made from the roots of the
       <a href="/wiki/Kava" title="Kava">
        kava
       </a>
       ; and the chewing of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Betel_nut" title="Betel nut">
        betel nuts
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       The traditional government system still influences the nation's affairs, leading the federal government to repeatedly attempt to limit its power. Many of these attempts took the form of amendments to the constitution that were supported by the corporate sector to protect what they deemed should be free economic zones.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2017)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       One such example occurred in early 2010, where the Idid clan, the ruling clan of the Southern Federation, under the leadership of Bilung, the Southern Federation's queen, raised a civil suit against the Koror State Public Lands Authority (KSPLA). The Idid clan laid claim over Malakal Island, a major economic zone and Palau's most important port, citing documents from the German Era. The verdict held that the Island belonged to the KSPLA.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Traditional_government">
        Traditional government
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Palau&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Traditional government">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       The present day "traditional" government of Palau is a continuation of its ancestor, composed of practices that span thousands of years.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2016)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       Traditionally, Palau was hierarchically organized. The lowest level is the village or hamlet, then the chiefdom (now politically referred to as a state) and finally alliances of chiefdoms. In ancient times, numerous federations divided power, but upon the 17th century introduction of firearms by the British, an imbalance of power occurred.
      </p>
      <p>
       Palau became divided into northern and southern federations. The Northern Federation is headed by the high chief and chiefess of the ruling clan Uudes of Melekeok state, the Reklai and Ebilreklai. They are commonly referred to as the king and queen of the Northern Federation. This northern federation comprises the state of Kayangel, Ngerchelong, Ngardmau, Ngiwal, Ngaraard, Ngatpang, Ngeremlengui, Melekok, Aimeliik, Ngchesar and Airai. The Southern Federation is likewise represented by the high chief and chiefess of the ruling Idid of Koror state.
      </p>
      <p>
       The Southern Federation comprises the states of Koror, Peleliu and Angaur. However, fewer and fewer Palauans have knowledge of the concept of federations, and the term is slowly dying out. Federations were established as a way of safeguarding states and hamlets who shared economic, social, and political interests, but with the advent a federal government, safeguards are less meaningful. It is interesting to note however, that in international relations, the king of Palau is synonymous with the Ibedul of Koror. This is because Koror is the industrial capital of the nation, elevating his position over the Reklai of Melekeok.
      </p>
      <p>
       It is a misconception that the king and queen of Palau, or any chief and his female counterpart for that matter are married. Traditional leaders and their female counterparts have always been related and unmarried (marrying relatives was a traditional taboo). Usually, a chief and his female counterpart are brother and sister, or close cousins, and have their own spouses.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">
        Sports
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Palau&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Sports">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a href="/wiki/Baseball_in_Palau" title="Baseball in Palau">
        Baseball in Palau
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Baseball" title="Baseball">
        Baseball
       </a>
       is a popular sport in Palau after its introduction by the Japanese in the 1920s. The
       <a href="/wiki/Palau_national_baseball_team" title="Palau national baseball team">
        Palau national baseball team
       </a>
       won the gold medal at the
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=1990_Micronesian_Games&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="1990 Micronesian Games (page does not exist)">
        1990
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=1998_Micronesian_Games&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="1998 Micronesian Games (page does not exist)">
        1998
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/2010_Micronesian_Games" title="2010 Micronesian Games">
        2010 Micronesian Games
       </a>
       , as well as at the
       <a href="/wiki/2007_Pacific_Games" title="2007 Pacific Games">
        2007 Pacific Games
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Palau also has a
       <a href="/wiki/Palau_national_football_team" title="Palau national football team">
        national football team
       </a>
       , organised by the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Palau_Soccer_Association" title="Palau Soccer Association">
        Palau Soccer Association
       </a>
       , but is not a member of
       <a href="/wiki/FIFA" title="FIFA">
        FIFA
       </a>
       . The Association also organizes the
       <a href="/wiki/Palau_Soccer_League" title="Palau Soccer League">
        Palau Soccer League
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Education">
        Education
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Palau&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Education">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Primary education is required until age of 16. Schools include both public and private institutions as well as some fields of study available at
       <a href="/wiki/Palau_Community_College" title="Palau Community College">
        Palau Community College
       </a>
       . For further undergraduate, graduate and professional programs, students travel abroad to attend tertiary institutions. Popular choices among Palauan scholars include the
       <a href="/wiki/San_Diego_State_University" title="San Diego State University">
        San Diego State University
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/University_of_the_South_Pacific" title="University of the South Pacific">
        University of the South Pacific
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52">
        <a href="#cite_note-52">
         [52]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <table class="mbox-small plainlinks sistersitebox" role="presentation" style="background-color:#f9f9f9;border:1px solid #aaa;color:#000">
       <tr>
        <td class="mbox-image">
         <img alt="" class="noviewer" data-file-height="415" data-file-width="759" height="22" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Wikinews-logo.svg/40px-Wikinews-logo.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Wikinews-logo.svg/60px-Wikinews-logo.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Wikinews-logo.svg/80px-Wikinews-logo.svg.png 2x" width="40"/>
        </td>
        <td class="mbox-text plainlist">
         Wikinews has related news:
         <i>
          <b>
           <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wikinews.org/wiki/Bones_of_%22small-bodied_humans%22_found_in_cave" title='wikinews:Bones of "small-bodied humans" found in cave'>
            Bones of "small-bodied humans" found in cave
           </a>
          </b>
         </i>
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">
        Cuisine
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Palau&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Cuisine">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_Oceanian_cuisines" title="List of Oceanian cuisines">
        List of Oceanian cuisines
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       Palau has its own cuisine, for instance, a dessert called
       <i>
        tama
       </i>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53">
        <a href="#cite_note-53">
         [53]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Palauan cuisine includes local foods such as
       <a href="/wiki/Cassava" title="Cassava">
        cassava
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Taro" title="Taro">
        taro
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Yam_(vegetable)" title="Yam (vegetable)">
        yam
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Potato" title="Potato">
        potato
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Fish" title="Fish">
        fish
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Pork" title="Pork">
        pork
       </a>
       .
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Western_cuisine" title="Western cuisine">
        Western cuisine
       </a>
       is favored among young Palauans.
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span id="In_art.2C_film_and_television">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="In_art,_film_and_television">
        In art, film and television
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Palau&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: In art, film and television">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       Several television programs and films have been shot in Palau. Examples include the reality show
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Survivor:_Palau" title="Survivor: Palau">
         Survivor: Palau
        </a>
       </i>
       and the 1968 film
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Hell_in_the_Pacific" title="Hell in the Pacific">
         Hell in the Pacific
        </a>
       </i>
       starring
       <a href="/wiki/Lee_Marvin" title="Lee Marvin">
        Lee Marvin
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54">
        <a href="#cite_note-54">
         [54]
        </a>
       </sup>
       A television documentary about Palau,
       <i>
        <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Strategic_Trust:_The_Making_of_Nuclear-free_Palau&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Strategic Trust: The Making of Nuclear-free Palau (page does not exist)">
         Strategic Trust: The Making of Nuclear-free Palau
        </a>
       </i>
       , was narrated by
       <a href="/wiki/Joanne_Woodward" title="Joanne Woodward">
        Joanne Woodward
       </a>
       and aired in the United States in 1984.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55">
        <a href="#cite_note-55">
         [55]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Graphic artist
       <a href="/wiki/Rolf_Weijburg" title="Rolf Weijburg">
        Rolf Weijburg
       </a>
       produced a colour etch of Turtle Cove, a dive site in Palau.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56">
        <a href="#cite_note-56">
         [56]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57">
        <a href="#cite_note-57">
         [57]
        </a>
       </sup>
       .
      </p>

         <span class="reference-text">
          <cite class="citation news">
           <a class="external text" href="https://www.webcitation.org/query?url=http%3A%2F%2Faustralianetworknews.com%2Fstories%2F201001%2F2804280.htm%3Fdesktop&amp;date=2010-02-04" rel="nofollow">
            "Palau receives aid boost from US"
           </a>
           .
           <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Australia_Network_News&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Australia Network News (page does not exist)">
            Australia Network News
           </a>
           . 30 January 2010. Archived from
           <a class="external text" href="http://australianetworknews.com/stories/201001/2804280.htm?desktop" rel="nofollow">
            the original
           </a>
           on 4 February 2010.
           <q>
            The president insisted there was no link to the island's hosting of six inmates from Guantanamo Bay. Palau had earlier rejected a 156 million dollar offer and the settlement came after the island nation agreed to resettle six Muslim Uighurs who had been held for more than seven years at the US naval base at Guantanamo Bay. The six arrived in Palau in November. But Johnson said the two issues were not related.
